Jamison Brereton

92 (701)
Indra
┼Ъrutakakс╣гa ─Ас╣Еgirasa or Sukakс╣гa ─Ас╣Еgirasa
33 verses: g─Бyatr─л, except anuс╣гс╣нubh 1, arranged in trcas ╠е
This long, loosely structured hymn is essentially a constantly repeated invitation to Indra to come to the soma sacrifice. Although the poet does ask for aid from time to time, the focus is on the sacrifice, the verbal accompaniments, and the soma itself. The poet names himself (or nicknames himself: the name is ┼Ъrutakakс╣гa тАЬhaving a famous armpitтАЭ [or a famous crotch]) in verse 25. This nickname appears in the midst of a striking sequence using the adverb ├бram тАЬfitting(ly)тАЭ (vss. 24тАУ27) in a clever shift implicitly equating IndraтАЩs body parts (e.g., тАЬfit for your cheekтАЭ vs. 24a) with the gifts the poet hopes to receive (e.g., тАЬfit for a horseтАЭ vs. 25a), at least once punningly: verse 35c, where the word dh─Б╠Бmane can refer both to a body part, the тАЬfundament,тАЭ that is, the buttocks, and to IndraтАЩs conferring of gifts.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSing priests, that Indra, who drinks your offered Soma– the foe- subduing ┼Ъatakratu, most liberal ofmen.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Or, to be most honoured of men, maс╣Гhiс╣гс╣нha carс╣гaс╣З─лn─Бm

Jamison Brereton

Sing (him) here to the drinking of your stalk; sing forth to Indra, the all-conquering one, of a hundred resolves, most liberal to the settled domains,

Jamison Brereton Notes

I separate the predicates of p─Бdas a and b because тИЪg─Б тАШsingтАЩ seems to be used in two different senses, with two different sets of preverbs: ─Б╠Бin a, abh├н pr├б in b

  • the first тАЬsing (s.o.) to (come to) X [acc.],тАЭ the second тАЬsing to s.o.тАЭ p─Б╠Бntam here belongs to the nominal stem p─Б╠Бnta- тАШdrinkтАЩ, not the pres. part., but the coincidence of form may have led to some ambiguity.
Griffith

INVITE ye Indra with a song to drink your draught of Soma juice,
All-conquering Satakratu, most munificent of all who live.

Geldner

Zu eurem Tranke des Soma ladet den Indra mit Gesang ein, den All├╝berwinder, den Ratreichen, der den V├╢lkern am meisten schenkt!

Grassmann

Auf, singt dem Indra Lobgesang, ihm, der von eurem Soma trinkt, Der thatenreich dass All bezwingt, der aller Geber bester ist.

English translation:

тАЬMay Indra who causes all to rejoice, be the giver of plural ntiful food to us; may be, the mighty, bring us(riches) up to our knees.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Who causes all to rejoice: nс╣Ыtuс╕е = nartayit─Б, he who causes all to dance; RV 2.22.4;bringer (neta) of kine to your votaries

Jamison Brereton

ItтАЩs Indra who is the giver to us of great prizes, the dancer.
The great one, in a crouch [=driving posture], will guide (the
prizes) here.

Jamison Brereton Notes

What posture abhij├▒├║ designates is not clear. Geldner thinks it involves bending the knees and sinking down, Scarlatta (345) that Indra crouches down because he is so large. I think rather that, as in I.37.10, it indicates a slightly crouching position, with knees bent, for driving a chariot (note I.37.10 abhij├▒├║ y─Б╠Бtave тАЬabhij├▒u to driveтАЭ), in this case to bring the prizes to us. The word nс╣Ыt├║с╕е тАШdancerтАЩ at the end of b is suggestive, so that abhij├▒u might instead, or also, be a dancing posture.

The first p─Бda of this new tс╣Ыca matches that of the first tс╣Ыca (1a): тИЪp─Б (p─Б╠Бntam (1a) / ├бp─Бt (4a) тАж ├бndhasaс╕е#.

├нndor ├нndro is an example of the word play, much beloved in IX, between ├нndu- тАШdropтАЩ and ├нndra-, but this case is particularly nice because sandhi allows the two words to be identical, save for the reversal of the final two sounds (or тИ╝ ro).

English translation:

тАЬThe god, having quaffed its exhilarations, by the strength of the divine (Soma) has conquered allworlds.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Having drunk of this god here, of his exhilarating drinks, the god with his power
will surmount all beings.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The two gods are, of course, Soma and Indra respectively.

Griffith

When he hath drqnk its gladdening drops, the God with vigour of a God
Hath far surpassed all things that are.

English translation:

тАЬBring here for our protection Indra the conqueror of many, who pervades all your praises.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

с╣Ъca isaddressed by the sacrificer to the praising priest

Jamison Brereton

Him, entirely victorious, held in place amid all your hymns
you will rouse for helpтАФ

Jamison Brereton Notes

IтАЩm not entirely sure of the sense of ─Б╠Бyatam in b. Geldner tr. тАЬauf alle Lobreden GespanntenтАЭ (intent on / excited about), which makes nice contextual sense, but which I find difficult to reconcile with the other occurrences of ─Б╠БтИЪyam, including, in this hymn, ─Б╠Бyamat in 3c and (abh├н) тАж ─Б╠Бyaman in 31b. Elsewhere ─Б╠БтИЪyam means тАШto hold (reins, etc.), hold fast, guideтАЩ. Here the sense may be that Indra is held (that is, kept) at the sacrifice by our songs, and there is then a contrast between his (temporary) immobility and the rousing we hope to give him (c: ─Б╠Бcy─Бvayasi).

Griffith

Thou speedest down to succour us this ever-conquering God of yours,
Him who is drawn to all our songs

Diesen vollst├дndig Besiegenden auf alle Lobreden Gespannten ziehst du f├╝r euch zur Gnade heran;

Grassmann

Ihn, euren allbezwingenden, den man zu allen Liedern lenkt, Ihn treibest du zur H├╝lfe her,

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe warrior, whom none oppose and none can harm, the quaffer of the Soma, the leader whose deedscannot be hindered.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The soma-drinker who is an unassailable fighter who cannot be budged, a superior man of unobstructable resolve.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This verse then showcases a different kind of immobility for Indra: ├бnapacyuta- тАШunbudgeableтАЩ; Indra here is not held, as it were, against his will, as perhaps in 7b, but because of his immense power he cannot be moved by lesser powers. Since in the immediately preceding verse (7c) the hope was to cause him to stir (тИЪcyu [cy─Бvayasi]), it is striking that here it is asserted that he cannot be made to тИЪcyu. (The relationship between these two forms should probably have been signaled in the Engl: perhaps тАЬyou rouse … unrousable.тАЭ) On the cmpd av─Бry├б-kratu- тАШpossessing unobstructable resolveтАЩ, see comm. ad IX.98.12.

Griffith

The Warrior not to he restrained, the Soma-drinker ne’er o’erthrown,
The Chieftain of resistless might.

Geldner

Der der unerreichte K├дmpfer ist, den unentwegten Somatrinker, den Herrn, der sich von seinem Willen nicht abbringen l├д├Яt.

Grassmann

Den K├дmpfer, der unnahbar ist, ein Somatrinker nimmersatt, Ein Mann von unbezwungner Kraft.

English translation:

тАЬ┼Ъakra, let us go, proved in deeds, to deeds; thunderer, cleaver of mountains, let us conquer in battlesby your steeds.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Steeds: by steeds given by you

Jamison Brereton

LetтАЩs go to the visionary thoughts of our visionary poet; with (the thoughts as) our steeds, o able one who breaks out the cows,
might we conquer in battles, o possessor of the mace.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Oldenberg and Geldner take ├бy─Бma as expletive тАЬletтАЩs go!тАЭ and construe the rest of the verse with j├бyema in c (тАЬmight we conquer the poems of the poet тАжтАЭ). Although this is possible, it requires the poet (dh─л╠Бvant-) in question to be a rival poet (so explicitly Oldenberg), and I wonder if we would flatteringly refer to a rival poet as тАЬvisionary.тАЭ I think rather that we are appropriating the visionary thoughts of our own poet and configuring them as steeds for vicotry in battle. For dh─л╠Б- = ├бrvant- cf. VI.45.12 dh─лbh├нr ├бrvadbhiс╕е … jeс╣гma тАЬWith visionary thoughts as our steeds might we conquer тАжтАЭ Construing ├бy─Бma with acc. of goal is very similar to ├бganma тАж ─Б┼Ы├бsaс╕е тАЬwe have arrived at our hopesтАЭ in 13c.

Griffith

We sought the wisdom of the wise. Sakra, Kine-giver, Thunder-armed!
May we with steeds o’ercome in fight.

Geldner

Wohlan! Wir wollen die Dichtungen des Dichtenden wie mit Rennpferden in den K├дmpfen besiegen, du m├дchtiger, Rinder herausschlagender Keulentr├дger.

Grassmann

Lass, starker Spender, Schleuderer, uns kommen zu des Frommen Werk Zu Ross, und siegen in der Schlacht.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWe refresh you, ┼Ъatakratu, with our praises, as (the herdsman) the cattle with (different kinds of)paasture.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

We will make you take pleasure in our hymns, o you of a hundred resolves,
as cows do in their pastures.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Case disharmony between simile and frame, as discussed in Jamison 1982, faciliated by the syntactic ambivanence of raс╣З├бya-, which has both causative and non-causative uses. Here the frame is causative, тАЬwe make you take pleasure in hymnsтАЭ (vay├бm u tv─Б тАж ukth├йс╣гu raс╣Зay─Бmasi), while the simile is non-causative, тАЬas cows (do) in grainтАЭ (g─Б╠Бvo n├б y├бvaseс╣гv ─Б╠Б).

Griffith

We make thee, Satakratu, find enjoyment in the songs we sing.
Like cattle in the pasture lands.

Geldner

Wir machen dich, du Ratreicher, der Loblieder froh wie K├╝he der Weide.

Grassmann

Wir schaffen, dass an Spr├╝chen du, o thatenreicher dich erlabst, Wie K├╝he an dem Wiesengras.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAll mortal natures, ┼Ъatakratu, are moved by desire; we feel wishes, O thunderer.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Because all things in the mortal way are in accord with your desire, o you of a hundred resolves,
we have arrived at our hopes, possessor of the mace.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner takes anuk─Бm─Б╠Бas тАШin accord with our desiresтАЩ, but it seems to me unlikely that we are claiming that everything goes as we want it; rather that man proposes, Indra disposes, and in this case he has disposed as we had hoped. This is supported by vs. 14 also, where the desirous ones turn to Indra (for him to fulfill their desires, presumably).

Griffith

For, Satakratu, Thunder-armed, all that we craved, as men are wont,
All that we hoped, have we attained.

Geldner

Denn alles ging nach Menschenart unseren W├╝nschen entsprechend, o Ratreicher; wir haben unsere Hoffnungen erreicht, o Keulentr├дger.

Grassmann

Es ist ja aller Menschen Art begehrlich, o vielwirkender, Uns kam das W├╝nschen an, o Held.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬO son of strength, men, uttering their desires, abide happily in you, none, Indra, surpasses you.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

To you, o son of strength, the desirers of desires have turned. Nothing surpasses you, Indra.

Griffith

Those, Son of Strength, are come to thee who cherish wishes in their hearts
O Indra, none excelleth thee.

Keith

To thee, O son of strength, they turn
Who have desires to be fulfilled;
None excelleth thee, O Indra.

Es wandten sich, o Herr der Kraft, zu dir sogleich die w├╝nschenden; Nichts ├╝berragt, o Indra, dich.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬShowerer (of blessings), protect us by your action, which is most bounteous yet awful, foe-terrifying yetmany-cherishing.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Purandhy─Б = bah┼лn─Бm dh─Бrayitry─Б; (RV 5.35.8): no ratham ava purandhy─Б =┼Ыobhanabudhy─Б; Showerer, protect us by your care, by your good providence, which is bounteous and yetawful and foe-terrifying

Jamison Brereton

O bull, give aid to us with the awesome, dashing
visionary thought that gains the most, and with plenitude.

Griffith

So, Hero, guard us with thy care, with thy most liberal providence,
Speedy, and terrible to foes.

Geldner

Steh uns bei, du Bulle, im Verein mit der gewinnbringendsten, furchtgebietenden, schnellen Dhi, mit der Purandhi, der Wunscherf├╝llung!

Grassmann

Drum hilf mit reichlichst spendender, mit herrlicher, mit eilender Beachtung und Versorgung uns.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On kukс╣г├н- as originally тАШcheekтАЩ, not тАШbellyтАЩ, see Jamison 1987; also for the pun on dh─Б╠Бman- тАШfoundationтАЩ, hence тАШfundamentтАЩ, that is, тАШbuttocks, bottomтАЩ, in vs. 24, but, in vs. 25, тАШfoundation, establishmentтАЩ in the sense of тАШbestowalтАЩ; also the jocular name ┼Ъrutakakс╣гa in 25.

24-27 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

The syntagm ├бram + DAT displays surprisingly complex semantics; there is generally a relationship of benefit between the subject and the dative, but which one receives the benefit is not fixed. We can see the shift in these vss., which contain a surprising number of such constructions: 2x in 24, 3x in 25, 2x in 26, 1x in 27. In 24 the beneficiary is expressed in the dative: the soma is beneficial to these parts of Indra, but in 27 the singer, who is the subject, by his action (singing) receives the benefits expressed in the three datives. The switch is esp. clever because in 24c the dative dh─Б╠Бmabhyaс╕е refers (by my interpr.) to a body part of IndraтАЩs, which benefits from the soma drops, but the same dative (save for number), ├нndrasya dh─Б╠Бmane, in 25c refers more likely (again in my interpr.) to a benefit that Indra will bestow (though the reading of 24c is also simultaneously possible). This change in focus is made clear (тАЬrepaired) in 26c, ├бram тАж d─Бv├бne тАЬfit(tingly) for (IndraтАЩs) giving,тАЭ which makes explicit the implication of 25c ├бram тАж dh─Б╠Бmane. Geldner (also Bloomfield Rig-Veda Repetitions) supplies тАЬweтАЭ as implicit subj. of c: тАЬ(wir sind) bereit f├╝r deine Schenkung,тАЭ but the playful parallelism with 24c seems to me to exclude this interpretation. The heavy phrase in 29 тАж r─Бt├нс╕е тАж dh─Бyi dh─Бtс╣Ы╠Бbhiс╕е тАЬ(IndraтАЩs) giving has been ordained by the ordainersтАЭ also establishes the link between IndraтАЩs giving and the root тИЪdh─Б.

The final ├бram in 27c returns us to the situation found in 24, where the provider of benefit is the subject (тАЬweтАЭ) and the beneficiary in the dative (тАЬyouтАЭ). I would now change the tr. to make that clearer: тАЬWe should go (to be) fit for you.тАЭ On the particular construction here, ├бram тИЪgam DAT, see also comm. ad X.9.3.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On kukс╣г├н- as originally тАШcheekтАЩ, not тАШbellyтАЩ, see Jamison 1987; also for the pun on dh─Б╠Бman- тАШfoundationтАЩ, hence тАШfundamentтАЩ, that is, тАШbuttocks, bottomтАЩ, in vs. 24, but, in vs. 25, тАШfoundation, establishmentтАЩ in the sense of тАШbestowalтАЩ; also the jocular name ┼Ъrutakakс╣гa in 25.

24-27 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

The syntagm ├бram + DAT displays surprisingly complex semantics; there is generally a relationship of benefit between the subject and the dative, but which one receives the benefit is not fixed. We can see the shift in these vss., which contain a surprising number of such constructions: 2x in 24, 3x in 25, 2x in 26, 1x in 27. In 24 the beneficiary is expressed in the dative: the soma is beneficial to these parts of Indra, but in 27 the singer, who is the subject, by his action (singing) receives the benefits expressed in the three datives. The switch is esp. clever because in 24c the dative dh─Б╠Бmabhyaс╕е refers (by my interpr.) to a body part of IndraтАЩs, which benefits from the soma drops, but the same dative (save for number), ├нndrasya dh─Б╠Бmane, in 25c refers more likely (again in my interpr.) to a benefit that Indra will bestow (though the reading of 24c is also simultaneously possible). This change in focus is made clear (тАЬrepaired) in 26c, ├бram тАж d─Бv├бne тАЬfit(tingly) for (IndraтАЩs) giving,тАЭ which makes explicit the implication of 25c ├бram тАж dh─Б╠Бmane. Geldner (also Bloomfield Rig-Veda Repetitions) supplies тАЬweтАЭ as implicit subj. of c: тАЬ(wir sind) bereit f├╝r deine Schenkung,тАЭ but the playful parallelism with 24c seems to me to exclude this interpretation. The heavy phrase in 29 тАж r─Бt├нс╕е тАж dh─Бyi dh─Бtс╣Ы╠Бbhiс╕е тАЬ(IndraтАЩs) giving has been ordained by the ordainersтАЭ also establishes the link between IndraтАЩs giving and the root тИЪdh─Б.

The final ├бram in 27c returns us to the situation found in 24, where the provider of benefit is the subject (тАЬweтАЭ) and the beneficiary in the dative (тАЬyouтАЭ). I would now change the tr. to make that clearer: тАЬWe should go (to be) fit for you.тАЭ On the particular construction here, ├бram тИЪgam DAT, see also comm. ad X.9.3.

English translation:

тАЬMay our praises reach you, thunderer, even from afar; may we obtain your (wealth) abundantly.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Even from a distance our hymns reach you, possessor of the stone. Let us go fittingly to you. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes
24-27 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

The syntagm ├бram + DAT displays surprisingly complex semantics; there is generally a relationship of benefit between the subject and the dative, but which one receives the benefit is not fixed. We can see the shift in these vss., which contain a surprising number of such constructions: 2x in 24, 3x in 25, 2x in 26, 1x in 27. In 24 the beneficiary is expressed in the dative: the soma is beneficial to these parts of Indra, but in 27 the singer, who is the subject, by his action (singing) receives the benefits expressed in the three datives. The switch is esp. clever because in 24c the dative dh─Б╠Бmabhyaс╕е refers (by my interpr.) to a body part of IndraтАЩs, which benefits from the soma drops, but the same dative (save for number), ├нndrasya dh─Б╠Бmane, in 25c refers more likely (again in my interpr.) to a benefit that Indra will bestow (though the reading of 24c is also simultaneously possible). This change in focus is made clear (тАЬrepaired) in 26c, ├бram тАж d─Бv├бne тАЬfit(tingly) for (IndraтАЩs) giving,тАЭ which makes explicit the implication of 25c ├бram тАж dh─Б╠Бmane. Geldner (also Bloomfield Rig-Veda Repetitions) supplies тАЬweтАЭ as implicit subj. of c: тАЬ(wir sind) bereit f├╝r deine Schenkung,тАЭ but the playful parallelism with 24c seems to me to exclude this interpretation. The heavy phrase in 29 тАж r─Бt├нс╕е тАж dh─Бyi dh─Бtс╣Ы╠Бbhiс╕е тАЬ(IndraтАЩs) giving has been ordained by the ordainersтАЭ also establishes the link between IndraтАЩs giving and the root тИЪdh─Б.

The final ├бram in 27c returns us to the situation found in 24, where the provider of benefit is the subject (тАЬweтАЭ) and the beneficiary in the dative (тАЬyouтАЭ). I would now change the tr. to make that clearer: тАЬWe should go (to be) fit for you.тАЭ On the particular construction here, ├бram тИЪgam DAT, see also comm. ad X.9.3.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Klein (318) takes ut├б as linking ┼Ы┼л╠Бraс╕е and sthir├бс╕е тАЬCertainly (thou art) heroic and firm,тАЭ but this assumes that ┼Ы┼л╠Бra- can be adjectival, which, pace Grassmann, I donтАЩt. Instead, despite its position, I take the ut├б as conjoining v─лray├║с╕е and ┼Ы┼л╠Бraс╕е тАж sthir├бс╕е, a variant on the complementary pairing of v─лr├б- тАШheroтАЩ and ┼Ы┼л╠Бra- тАШchampionтАЩ.

28-29 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner tr. r─Б╠Бdhya- as тАЬleicht zu gewinnen,тАЭ but I take it rather as тАЬto be realized, brought to success.тАЭ What the content of IndraтАЩs thought is may be clarified by V.39.3 y├бt te dits├║ prar─Б╠Бdhyam m├бnaс╕е … тАЬyour thought … which is eager to give, should be realized.тАЭ The giving theme is made explicit in the next verse. His intention (the m├бnas- of 28c) is to give, and this intention will be realized, because giving (r─Бt├н-, 29a) has been ordained as part of his nature. Then 29c reaffirms the ritual partnership of mutual giving between Indra and his worshipers. I consider GeldnerтАЩs тАЬund doch (bist du), Indra, bei mirтАЭ not sufficiently specific, esp. given the strong assertion of connection between us and Indra in the tv─Б╠Бyuj─Б╠Б(31c), tv├бy├йd тАж yuj─Б╠Б (32c) тАЬwith you as yokemateтАЭ found in following verses, not to mention 32c tv├бm asm─Б╠Бkaс╣Г t├бva smasi тАЬYou are ours; we are yours.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner tr. r─Б╠Бdhya- as тАЬleicht zu gewinnen,тАЭ but I take it rather as тАЬto be realized, brought to success.тАЭ What the content of IndraтАЩs thought is may be clarified by V.39.3 y├бt te dits├║ prar─Б╠Бdhyam m├бnaс╕е … тАЬyour thought … which is eager to give, should be realized.тАЭ The giving theme is made explicit in the next verse. His intention (the m├бnas- of 28c) is to give, and this intention will be realized, because giving (r─Бt├н-, 29a) has been ordained as part of his nature. Then 29c reaffirms the ritual partnership of mutual giving between Indra and his worshipers. I consider GeldnerтАЩs тАЬund doch (bist du), Indra, bei mirтАЭ not sufficiently specific, esp. given the strong assertion of connection between us and Indra in the tv─Б╠Бyuj─Б╠Б(31c), tv├бy├йd тАж yuj─Б╠Б (32c) тАЬwith you as yokemateтАЭ found in following verses, not to mention 32c tv├бm asm─Б╠Бkaс╣Г t├бva smasi тАЬYou are ours; we are yours.тАЭ

English translation:

тАЬIndra,let not the threatening prowling (demons) obstruct us at night, let us smite them with you as ourhelper.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Let not (ill) intentions toward us guide us away from the sun into the nights, Indra.
With you as yokemate, we would gain it.

Jamison Brereton Notes

A difficult hemistich, whose uncertainties include the function of abh├н, the meaning of ─Б╠Бyaman, and the grammatical identity and use of s┼л╠Бraс╕е. Contra Grassmann I do not take abh├н as another preverb with ─Б╠БтИЪyam. The only other example of abh├н-─Б╠Б тИЪyam is in a gerundive in a curious idiom in an A┼Ыvin hymn (I.34.1). Moreover, if it is a preverb, it has taken an odd position: we generally find preverbs in tmesis at the beginnings of p─Бdas. I instead take it as governing naс╕е. As for ─Б╠Бyaman, it needs to be considered in connection with other ─Б╠БтИЪyam forms in this hymn, particularly ─Б╠Бyamat in 3c (also ─Б╠Бyatam 7b). In 3c the lexeme means тАШguideтАЩ, and I take it so here as well, with naс╕е (read twice) as its object. In this interpretation s┼л╠Бraс╕е is ablative of sv├аr, rather than gen. to this stem (Grassmann, Oldenberg, with the latter suggesting it might be a temporal gen.) or nom. sg. to s┼л╠Бra- (Geldner).

In c the referent of t├бt is not specified. Geldner thinks itтАЩs the sun, which is certainly possible.

Griffith

O Indra, let not ill designs surround us in the sunbeams’ light:
This may we gain with thee for Friend.

Geldner

Nicht sollen, Indra, die Drohungen auf uns abzielen, wenn die Sonne im Dunkeln ist. Mit dir im Bunde wollen wir diese gewinnen.

Grassmann

Nicht ziele bei der Sonne Strahl auf uns, o Indra, b├╢se List, Durch deine Huld gew├дhr uns das.
